title=".ms">.ms</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Montserrat</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> (BOT) in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>. The island is in the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands" title="Leeward Islands">Leeward Islands</a>, which is part of the chain known as the <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">Lesser Antilles</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a>. Montserrat measures approximately 16&#160;km (10&#160;mi) in length and 11&#160;km (7&#160;mi) in width, with approximately 40&#160;km (25&#160;mi) of coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Montserrat is nicknamed "The Emerald Isle of the Caribbean" both for its resemblance to coastal <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish ancestry</a> of many of its inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes-7">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes-video_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes-video-8">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 18 July 1995, the previously <a href="/wiki/Dormant_volcano" class="mw-redirect" title="Dormant volcano">dormant</a> <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière Hills">Soufrière Hills</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, in the southern part of the island, became active. Eruptions destroyed Montserrat's <a href="/wiki/Georgian_era" title="Georgian era">Georgian era</a> capital city of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">Plymouth</a>. Between 1995 and 2000, two-thirds of the island's population was forced to flee, primarily to the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, leaving fewer than 1,200 people on the island as of 1997 (rising to nearly 5,000 by 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-mvo.ms_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mvo.ms-9">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016Pop_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The volcanic activity continues, mostly affecting the vicinity of Plymouth, including its docking facilities, and the eastern side of the island around the former <a href="/wiki/W._H._Bramble_Airport" title="W. H. Bramble Airport">W. H. Bramble Airport</a>, the remnants of which were buried by flows from volcanic activity on 11 February 2010.
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Exclusion_zone#Natural_disaster_exclusion_zones" title="Exclusion zone">exclusion zone</a>, encompassing the southern half of the island to as far north as parts of the Belham Valley, was imposed because of the size of the existing volcanic dome and the resulting potential for <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastics" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyroclastics">pyroclastic</a> activity. Visitors are generally not permitted entry into the exclusion zone, but a view of the destruction of Plymouth can be seen from the top of Garibaldi Hill in Isles Bay. Relatively quiet since early 2010, the volcano continues to be closely monitored by the <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Volcano_Observatory" title="Montserrat Volcano Observatory">Montserrat Volcano Observatory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A new town and port are being developed at Little Bay, which is on the northwest coast of the island. While this construction proceeds, the centre of government and businesses is at <a href="/wiki/Brades" title="Brades">Brades</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1493, Christopher Columbus named the island <i>Santa María de Montserrate</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_of_Montserrat" title="Virgin of Montserrat">Virgin of Montserrat</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_de_Montserrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Maria de Montserrat">Monastery of Montserrat</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_(mountain)" title="Montserrat (mountain)">Montserrat mountain</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> "Montserrat" means "<a href="/wiki/Serration" title="Serration">serrated</a> mountain" in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/220px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/330px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif/440px-Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif 2x" data-file-width="1791" data-file-height="1791" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Soufriere_Hills_Volcano_dome_collapse.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>False-color time-lapse images of the Soufrière Hills volcanic dome collapse in 2010, from <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg/220px-Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg/330px-Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg/440px-Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plymouth_City_%26_Volcano.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Plymouth City and volcano</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Salem_Eruption1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Montserrat_Salem_Eruption1.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Salem_Eruption1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/eb/Montserrat_Salem_Eruption1.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="201" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Salem_Eruption1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eruption of the Soufrière Hills volcano on 22 September 1997</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/British_West_Indies" title="British West Indies">British West Indies</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_from_above,_Montserrat.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/220px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/330px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG/440px-Little_Bay_from_above%2C_Montserrat.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay_from_above,_Montserrat.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of half of the coastline of Little Bay, and a glimpse of Carrs Bay, taken from partway up the headland between Little Bay and Rendezvous Bay, 2012</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial_era">Pre-colonial era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Archaeological field work in 2012, in Montserrat's Centre Hills indicated there was an Archaic (pre-<a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a>) occupation between 4000 and 2500 <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">BP</a> (2000 - 500 BC).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Later coastal sites show the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Saladoid" title="Saladoid">Saladoid</a> culture (until 550 AD).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The native Caribs are believed to have called the island <i>Alliouagana</i>, meaning 'Land of the Prickly Bush'.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_European_period">Early European period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Early European period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 1493, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> passed Montserrat in his <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus#Caribbean_exploration" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">second voyage</a>, after being told that the island was unoccupied due to raids by the <a href="/wiki/Island_Caribs" title="Island Caribs">Caribs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A number of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Irishmen</a> <a href="/wiki/Irish_immigration_to_Montserrat" title="Irish immigration to Montserrat">settled in Montserrat in 1632</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Most came from nearby <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts">St Kitts</a> at the instigation of the island's governor <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Warner_(explorer)" title="Thomas Warner (explorer)">Thomas Warner</a>, with more settlers arriving later from <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The preponderance of Irish in the first wave of European settlers led a leading legal scholar to remark that a "nice question" is whether the original settlers took with them the law of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Kingdom of Ireland</a> insofar as it differed from the law of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Irish</a> being historical allies of the <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a>, especially in their dislike of the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a>, invited the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a> to claim the island in 1666, although no troops were sent by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to maintain control.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However the French did attack and briefly occupy the island in the late 1660s;<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> it was captured shortly afterwards by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> and English control of the island was confirmed under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda</a> the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Despite the seizing by force of the island by the <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">English</a>, the island's legal status is that of a "colony acquired by settlement".<sup id="cite_ref-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colonial_Law&#39;_1966._P._855-19">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Neofeudalism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neofeudalism">neo-feudal</a> colony developed amongst the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Redlegs" class="mw-redirect" title="Redlegs">redlegs</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The colonists began to transport <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Sub-Saharan African</a> slaves for labour, as was common to most <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> islands.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The colonists built an economy based on the production of sugar, <a href="/wiki/Rum" title="Rum">rum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arrowroot" title="Arrowroot">arrowroot</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sea_island_cotton" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea island cotton">sea island cotton</a>, cultivated on large plantations manned by slave labour. By the late 18th century, numerous <a href="/wiki/Plantations" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantations">plantations</a> had been developed on the island. Many Irish continued to be transported to the island, to work as indentured servants; some were exiled during the English <a href="/wiki/Cromwellian_conquest_of_Ireland" title="Cromwellian conquest of Ireland">Cromwellian conquest of Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-everyculture_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-everyculture-23">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There was a brief French attack on Montserrat in 1712.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On 17 March 1768, slaves rebelled but failed to achieve freedom.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The people of Montserrat celebrate <a href="/wiki/St_Patrick%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="St Patrick&#39;s Day">St Patrick's Day</a> as a public holiday due to the slave revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Festivities held that week commemorate the culture of Montserrat in song, dance, food and traditional costumes.
</p><p>In 1782, during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, as America's first ally, France <a href="/wiki/French_capture_of_Montserrat" class="mw-redirect" title="French capture of Montserrat">captured</a> Montserrat in their war of support of the Americans.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The French, not intent on truly colonising the island, then agreed to return the island to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">1783 Treaty of Paris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irish_language_in_Montserrat">Irish language in Montserrat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Irish language in Montserrat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Irish constituted the largest proportion of the white population from the founding of the colony in 1628. Many were indentured labourers; others were merchants or plantation owners. The geographer Thomas Jeffrey claimed in <i>The West India Atlas</i> (1780) that the majority of those on Montserrat were either Irish or of Irish descent, "so that the use of the <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish language</a> is preserved on the island, even among the Negroes".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>African slaves and Irish colonists of all classes were in constant contact, with sexual relationships being common and a population of mixed descent appearing as a consequence.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The Irish were also prominent in Caribbean commerce, with their merchants importing Irish goods such as beef, pork, butter and herring, and also importing slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There is indirect evidence that the use of the Irish language continued in Montserrat until at least the middle of the nineteenth century. The <a href="/wiki/County_Kilkenny" title="County Kilkenny">Kilkenny</a> diarist and Irish scholar <a href="/wiki/Amhlaoibh_%C3%93_S%C3%BAilleabh%C3%A1in" title="Amhlaoibh Ó Súilleabháin">Amhlaoibh Ó Súilleabháin</a> noted in 1831 that he had heard that Irish was still spoken in Montserrat by both black and white inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Bhaldraithe-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>in 1852, Henry H. Breen wrote in <i>Notes and Queries: a Medium of Intercommunication for Literary Men, etc.</i> that "The statement that “the Irish language is spoken in the West India Islands, and that in some of them it may be said to be almost vernacular,” is true of the little Island of Montserrat, but has no foundation with respect to the other colonies."<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1902, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Irish_Times" title="The Irish Times">The Irish Times</a></i> quoted the <i>Montreal Family Herald</i> in a description of Montserrat, noting that "the negroes to this day speak the old Irish Gaelic tongue, or English with an Irish brogue. A story is told of a <a href="/wiki/Connaught" class="mw-redirect" title="Connaught">Connaught</a> man who, on arriving at the island, was, to his astonishment, hailed in a vernacular Irish by the black people."<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A letter by W. F. Butler in <i>The Atheneum</i> (15 July 1905) quotes an account by a <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> civil servant, C. Cremen, of what he had heard from a retired sailor called John O'Donovan, a fluent Irish speaker:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>He frequently told me that in the year 1852, when mate of the brig Kaloolah, he went ashore on the island of Montserrat which was then out of the usual track of shipping. He said he was much surprised to hear the negroes actually talking Irish among themselves, and that he joined in the conversation…<sup id="cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Bhaldraithe-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p></blockquote>
<p>The British phonetician <a href="/wiki/John_C._Wells" title="John C. Wells">John C. Wells</a> conducted research into speech in Montserrat in 1977&#8211;78 (which included also Montserratians resident in London).<sup id="cite_ref-Wells_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He found media claims that Irish speech, whether <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Irish">Anglo-Irish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Irish_Gaelic" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Gaelic">Irish Gaelic</a>, influenced contemporary Montserratian speech were largely exaggerated.<sup id="cite_ref-Wells_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He found little in phonology, morphology or syntax that could be attributed to Irish influence, and in Wells' report, only a small number of Irish words in use, one example being <i>minseach</i> [ˈmʲiɲʃəx] which he suggests is the noun <i>goat</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wells_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wells-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> However as the word is an adjective and translates as having resolve, spirit, or <i>courage</i>, attributes that a ramming goat may have, the locals viewed Wells' particularly closed line of questioning, where the desired outcome was loaded into the question, as attempting to engage in confirmation bias and thus on recognizing the nature of Wells' intent, saw fit to play with describing him, or giving him exactly what he had set out to "prove".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_crops_and_politics">New crops and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: New crops and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Britain <a href="/wiki/Slavery_Abolition_Act_1833" title="Slavery Abolition Act 1833">abolished slavery</a> in Montserrat and its other territories effective August 1834.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto2_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto1_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-21">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the nineteenth century, falling sugar prices had an adverse effect on the island's economy, as <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and other nations competed in the trade.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1857, the British philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Sturge" title="Joseph Sturge">Joseph Sturge</a> bought a sugar estate to prove it was economically viable to employ paid labour rather than slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Numerous members of the Sturge family bought additional land. In 1869 the family established the Montserrat Company Limited and planted <a href="/wiki/Key_lime" title="Key lime">Key lime</a> trees, started the commercial production of lime juice, set up a school, and sold parcels of land to the inhabitants of the island. Much of Montserrat came to be owned by <a href="/wiki/Smallholding" title="Smallholding">smallholders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Connection_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Connection-38">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1871 to 1958, Montserrat was administered as part of the federal <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Leeward_Islands" title="British Leeward Islands">British Leeward Islands</a>, becoming a province of the short-lived <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Federation" title="West Indies Federation">West Indies Federation</a> from 1958 to 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Montserrat" title="Chief Minister of Montserrat">Chief Minister of Montserrat</a> was <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Bramble" title="William Henry Bramble">William Henry Bramble</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Labour_Party" title="Montserrat Labour Party">Montserrat Labour Party</a> from 1960 to 1970; he worked to promote labour rights and boost tourism to the island, and Montserrat's original airport was named in his honour.<sup id="cite_ref-source2_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-source2-41">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> However Bramble's son <a href="/wiki/Percival_Austin_Bramble" title="Percival Austin Bramble">Percival Austin Bramble</a> was critical of the way tourist facilities were being constructed, and he subsequently set up his own party (the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democratic_Party_(Montserrat)" title="Progressive Democratic Party (Montserrat)">Progressive Democratic Party</a>) which went on to win the <a href="/wiki/1970_Montserratian_general_election" title="1970 Montserratian general election">1970 Montserratian general election</a>, with Percival Bramble serving as Chief Minister from 1970-78.<sup id="cite_ref-RA_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RA-42">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The period 1978-1991 was dominated politically by Chief Minister <a href="/wiki/John_Osborne_(Montserrat_politician)" title="John Osborne (Montserrat politician)">John Osborne</a> and his <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Movement_(Montserrat)" title="People&#39;s Liberation Movement (Montserrat)">People's Liberation Movement</a>; his brief flirtation with possibly declaring independence never materialised.
</p><p>In 1979, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> producer <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a> opened <a href="/wiki/AIR_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="AIR Studios">AIR Studios Montserrat</a>, which resulted in musical artists such as <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Buffett" title="Jimmy Buffett">Jimmy Buffett</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> visiting the island to record albums.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Island_Sunset_(4568325551).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/330px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg/440px-Montserrat_Island_Sunset_%284568325551%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1739" data-file-height="1174" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Island_Sunset_(4568325551).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montserrat from the <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe_Passage" title="Guadeloupe Passage">Guadeloupe Passage</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the early hours of 17 September 1989, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> passed the island as a Category&#160;4 hurricane, damaging more than 90% of the structures on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_17-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-17">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> AIR Studios Montserrat closed, and the tourist economy was virtually wiped out.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Corruption allegations within the PLM party resulted in the collapse of the Osborne government in 1991, with <a href="/wiki/Reuben_Meade" title="Reuben Meade">Reuben Meade</a> becoming the new chief minister.<sup id="cite_ref-SA_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> As a result, early elections were called.<sup id="cite_ref-SA_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SA-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1995 Montserrat was devastated by the catastrophic volcanic eruptions of the Soufrière Hills, which destroyed the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">Plymouth</a>, and necessitated the evacuation of a large part of the island. Many Montserratians emigrated abroad, mainly to the United Kingdom, though in recent years some have started returning. The eruptions rendered the entire southern half of the island uninhabitable, and it is currently designated an Exclusion Zone with restricted access. Criticism of the Montserratian government's response to the disaster led to the resignation of Chief Minister <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Osborne" title="Bertrand Osborne">Bertrand Osborne</a> in 1997 after only a year in office, being replaced by <a href="/wiki/David_Brandt_(politician)" title="David Brandt (politician)">David Brandt</a> who remained in office until 2001. Since leaving office Brandt has been the subject of criminal investigation into alleged sex offences.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>John Osborne returned as Chief Minister following victory in the 2001 election, being ousted by <a href="/wiki/Lowell_Lewis" title="Lowell Lewis">Lowell Lewis</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Democratic_Party" title="Montserrat Democratic Party">Montserrat Democratic Party</a> in 2006. Ruben Meade returned to office in 2009-2014;<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> during his term the post of Chief Minister was replaced with that of <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Montserrat" title="Premier of Montserrat">Premier</a>. Since 2014 <a href="/wiki/Donaldson_Romeo" title="Donaldson Romeo">Donaldson Romeo</a>  of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Movement_(Montserrat)" title="People&#39;s Democratic Movement (Montserrat)">People's Democratic Movement</a> has been Premier. In the fall of 2017, Montserrat was not hit by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Hurricane Irma</a> and sustained only minor damage from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Montserrat" title="Politics of Montserrat">Politics of Montserrat</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:137px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Henry_Bramble.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/13/William_Henry_Bramble.jpg" decoding="async" width="135" height="213" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="135" data-file-height="213" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Henry_Bramble.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>William Henry Bramble, first Chief Minister of Montserrat, 1960-70</div></div></div>
<p>Montserrat is an internally self-governing <a href="/wiki/British_overseas_territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British overseas territory">overseas territory</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> Committee on Decolonization includes Montserrat on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a>. The island's Chief of State is <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> represented by an appointed Governor. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government, whereas the Premier is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. The Premier is appointed by the Governor from among the members of the Legislative Assembly which consists of nine elected members. The leader of the party with a majority of seats is usually the one who is appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Montserrat" title="Legislative Assembly of Montserrat">Legislative Assembly</a>. The Assembly also includes two <i><a href="/wiki/Ex_officio" class="mw-redirect" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> members, the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_general" title="Attorney general">attorney general</a> and financial secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Military defence is the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> so the island has no regular army.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">Judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature.
</p><p><i>Further information: <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Montserrat" title="Attorney General of Montserrat">Attorney General of Montserrat</a></i>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/170px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/255px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg/340px-Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="264" data-file-height="401" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parishes_of_Montserrat.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Montserrat's parishes: Saint Peter in the north, Saint Georges in the centre, and Saint Anthony in the south. The square marks Plymouth, the abandoned capital.</div></div></div>
<p>For the purposes of local government, Montserrat is divided into three <a href="/wiki/Parish_(administrative_division)" title="Parish (administrative division)">parishes</a>. Going north to south, they are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_Parish,_Montserrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Peter Parish, Montserrat">Saint Peter Parish</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Georges_Parish,_Montserrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Georges Parish, Montserrat">Saint Georges Parish</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saint_Anthony_Parish,_Montserrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Anthony Parish, Montserrat">Saint Anthony Parish</a></li></ul>
<p>The locations of settlements on the island have been vastly changed since the volcanic activity began. Only Saint Peter Parish in the northwest of the island is now inhabited, with a population of between 4,000 and 6,000,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> the other two parishes being still too dangerous to inhabit.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The island is served by landline telephones, fully digitalized, with 3,000 subscribers and by mobile cellular, with an estimated number of 5,000 handsets in use. An estimated 2,860 users have internet access. These are July 2016 estimates. Public radio service is provided by Radio Montserrat. There is a single television broadcaster, PTV.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Cable and satellite television service is available.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#British_Overseas_Territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK Postcode</a> for directing mail to Montserrat is MSR followed by four digits according to the destination town, for example, the postcode for Little Bay is MSR1120.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Coastal_cliffs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/220px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/330px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Coastal_cliffs.jpg/440px-Coastal_cliffs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Coastal_cliffs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Montserrat's coastline</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Montserrat" title="Geography of Montserrat">Geography of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>The island of Montserrat is located approximately 25 miles (39&#160;km) south-west of <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, 13m (22&#160;km) south-east of <a href="/wiki/Redonda" title="Redonda">Redonda</a> (a small island owned by <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>), and 35m (56&#160;km) north-west of the French overseas region of <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>. Beyond Redonda lies <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> (part of <a href="/wiki/St_Kitts_and_Nevis" class="mw-redirect" title="St Kitts and Nevis">St Kitts and Nevis</a>), about 30m (49&#160;km) to the north-west. It comprises 104&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (40&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is gradually increasing owing to the buildup of volcanic deposits on the south-east coast. The island is 16&#160;km (9.9&#160;mi) long and 11&#160;km (6.8&#160;mi) wide and consists of a mountainous interior surrounded by a flatter littoral region, with rock cliffs rising 15 to 30&#160;m (49 to 98&#160;ft) above the sea and a number of smooth bottomed sandy beaches scattered among <a href="/wiki/Cove" title="Cove">coves</a> on the western (Caribbean Sea) side of the island. The major mountains are (from north to south) <a href="/w/index.php?title=Silver_Hill,_Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Silver Hill, Montserrat (page does not exist)">Silver Hill</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Katy_Hill,_Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Katy Hill, Montserrat (page does not exist)">Katy Hill</a> in the Centre Hills range, the <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière Hills">Soufrière Hills</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=South_Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="South Soufrière Hills (page does not exist)">South Soufrière Hills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Soufrière Hills <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a> is the island's highest point; its pre-1995 height was 915m, however it has now grown due post-eruption due to the creation of a <a href="/wiki/Lava_dome" title="Lava dome">lava dome</a>, with its current height being estimated at 1,050m.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2011 estimate by the CIA indicates that 30% of the island's land is classified as agricultural, 20% as arable, 25% as forest and the balance as "other".<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montserrat has a few tiny off-shore islands, such as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Little_Redonda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Little Redonda (page does not exist)">Little Redonda</a> off its north coast and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pinnacle_Rock,_Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pinnacle Rock, Montserrat (page does not exist)">Pinnacle Rock</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Statue_Rock&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Statue Rock (page does not exist)">Statue Rock</a> off its east.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Volcano_and_exclusion_zone">Volcano and exclusion zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Volcano and exclusion zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_eruption.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/220px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/330px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Montserrat_eruption.JPG/440px-Montserrat_eruption.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_eruption.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Plymouth,_Montserrat" title="Plymouth, Montserrat">Plymouth</a>, the former capital city and major port of Montserrat, on 12 July 1997, after <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> burned much of what was not covered in ash</div></div></div>
<p>In July 1995, Montserrat's <a href="/wiki/Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Soufrière Hills">Soufrière Hills</a> <a href="/wiki/Volcano" title="Volcano">volcano</a>, dormant for centuries, erupted and soon buried the island's capital, Plymouth, in more than 12 metres (39&#160;ft) of mud, destroyed its airport and docking facilities, and rendered the southern part of the island, now termed the exclusion zone, uninhabitable and not safe for travel. The southern part of the island was evacuated and visits are severely restricted.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The exclusion zone also includes two sea areas adjacent to the land areas of most volcanic activity.<sup id="cite_ref-mvo.ms_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mvo.ms-9">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the destruction of Plymouth and disruption of the economy, more than half of the population left the island, which also lacked housing. During the late 1990s, additional eruptions occurred. On 25 June 1997, a pyroclastic flow travelled down Mosquito <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ghaut" class="extiw" title="wikt:ghaut">Ghaut</a>. This <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_surge" title="Pyroclastic surge">pyroclastic surge</a> could not be restrained by the <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ghaut" class="extiw" title="wikt:ghaut">ghaut</a> and spilled out of it, killing 19 people who were in the (officially evacuated) Streatham village area. Several others in the area suffered severe burns.
</p><p>For a number of years in the early 2000s, the volcano's activity consisted mostly of infrequent ventings of <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_ash" title="Volcanic ash">ash</a> into the uninhabited areas in the south. The ash falls occasionally extended into the northern and western parts of the island. In the most recent period of increased activity at the Soufrière Hills volcano, from November 2009 through February 2010, ash vented and there was a <a href="/wiki/Vulcanian_eruption" title="Vulcanian eruption">vulcanian explosion</a> that sent <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flow" title="Pyroclastic flow">pyroclastic flows</a> down several sides of the mountain. Travel into parts of the exclusion zone is occasionally allowed, though only by a licence from the Royal Montserrat Police Force.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The northern part of Montserrat has largely been unaffected by volcanic activity, and remains lush and green. In February 2005, <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">The Princess Royal</a> officially opened what is now called the <a href="/wiki/John_A._Osborne_Airport" title="John A. Osborne Airport">John A. Osborne Airport</a> in the north. Since 2011, it handles several flights daily operated by <a href="/wiki/FlyMontserrat" title="FlyMontserrat">Fly Montserrat Airways</a>. Docking facilities are in place at Little Bay, where the new capital town is being constructed; the new government centre is at Brades, a short distance away.
</p><p>In recognition of the disaster, in 1998, the people of Montserrat were granted full residency rights in the United Kingdom, allowing them to migrate if they chose. British citizenship was granted in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Montserrat" title="List of birds of Montserrat">List of birds of Montserrat</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Montserrat" title="List of mammals of Montserrat">List of mammals of Montserrat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_and_reptiles_of_Montserrat" title="List of amphibians and reptiles of Montserrat">List of amphibians and reptiles of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Montserrat, like many isolated islands, is home to rare, <a href="/wiki/Endemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Endemic">endemic</a> plant and animal species. Work undertaken by the Montserrat National Trust in collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a> has centred on the conservation of pribby (<i>Rondeletia buxifolia</i>) in the Centre Hills region. Until 2006, this species was known only from one book about the vegetation of Montserrat.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, conservationists also rescued several plants of the endangered Montserrat orchid (<i>Epidendrum montserratense</i>) from dead trees on the island and installed them in the security of the island's botanic garden.
</p><p>Montserrat is also home to the critically endangered <a href="/wiki/Leptodactylus_fallax" title="Leptodactylus fallax">giant ditch frog (<i>Leptodactylus fallax</i>)</a>, known locally as the mountain chicken, found only in Montserrat and <a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a>. The species has undergone catastrophic declines due to the amphibian disease <a href="/wiki/Chytridiomycosis" title="Chytridiomycosis">Chytridiomycosis</a> and the volcanic eruption in 1997. Experts from <a href="/wiki/Durrell_Wildlife_Conservation_Trust" title="Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust">Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust</a> have been working with the Montserrat Department of Environment to conserve the frog <a href="/wiki/In-situ_conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="In-situ conservation">in-situ</a> in a project called "Saving the Mountain Chicken",<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Ex-situ_conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ex-situ conservation">ex-situ</a> captive breeding population has been set up in partnership with Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust, <a href="/wiki/Zoological_Society_of_London" title="Zoological Society of London">Zoological Society of London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">North of England Zoological Society</a>, Parken Zoo and the Governments of Montserrat and Dominica. Releases from this programme have already taken place in a hope to increase the numbers of the frog and reduce extinction risk from Chytridiomycosis.
</p><p>The national bird is the endemic <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_oriole" title="Montserrat oriole">Montserrat oriole</a> (<i>Icterus oberi</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> classifies it as Vulnerable, having previously listed it as Critically Endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Captive populations are held in several zoos in the UK including: <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">Chester Zoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_Zoo" title="London Zoo">London Zoo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jersey_Zoo" title="Jersey Zoo">Jersey Zoo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Zoo" title="Edinburgh Zoo">Edinburgh Zoo</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_galliwasp" title="Montserrat galliwasp">Montserrat galliwasp</a> (<i>Diploglossus montisserrati</i>), a type of lizard, is endemic to Montserrat and is listed on the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> as Critically Endangered.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> A species action plan has been developed for this species.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, a biodiversity assessment for the Centre Hills was conducted. To support the work of local conservationists, a team of international partners, including <a href="/wiki/Durrell_Wildlife_Conservation_Trust" title="Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust">Durrell Wildlife Conservation Trust</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_for_the_Protection_of_Birds" title="Royal Society for the Protection of Birds">Royal Society for the Protection of Birds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Montana_State_University" title="Montana State University">Montana State University</a>, carried out extensive surveys and collected biological data.<sup id="cite_ref-durrell.org_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-durrell.org-66">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Researchers from Montana State University found that the invertebrate fauna was particularly rich on the island. The report found that the number of invertebrate species known to occur in Montserrat is 1,241. The number of known beetle species is 718 species from 63 families. It is estimated that 120 invertebrates are endemic to Montserrat.<sup id="cite_ref-durrell.org_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-durrell.org-66">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Montserrat is known for its coral reefs and its caves along the shore. These caves house many species of bats, and efforts are underway to monitor and protect the ten species of bats from extinction.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Montserrat Tarantula (<i><a href="/wiki/Cyrtopholis" title="Cyrtopholis">Cyrtopholis</a> femoralis</i>) is the only species of tarantula native to the island. It was first bred in captivity at the <a href="/wiki/Chester_Zoo" title="Chester Zoo">Chester Zoo</a> in August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caribe_Queen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/220px-Caribe_Queen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/330px-Caribe_Queen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Caribe_Queen.jpg/440px-Caribe_Queen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caribe_Queen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Motor_ship" title="Motor ship">MV</a> <i>Caribe Queen</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Nevis" title="Nevis">Nevis</a> ferry boat which shuttles passengers between <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> and Montserrat several times a week.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Montserrat" title="Economy of Montserrat">Economy of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Montserrat's economy was devastated by the 1995 eruption and its aftermath;<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_26-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> currently the island's operating budget is largely supplied by the British government and administered through the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a> (DFID) amounting to approximately £25 million per year. Additional amounts are secured through income and property taxes, licence and other fees as well as customs duties levied on imported goods.
</p><p>The limited economy of Montserrat, coupled with a population under 5,000, many living in shelters and shacks without utilities, only consumes 1.7 MW of electric power, produced by five diesel generators.<sup id="cite_ref-2016Pop_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Two exploratory <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_power" title="Geothermal power">geothermal wells</a> have found good resources and the pad for a third geothermal well was prepared in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Together the geothermal wells are expected to produce more power than the island requires.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A report published by the CIA indicated that the value of exports totaled the equivalent of US$5.7 million (2017 est.), consisting primarily of electronic components, plastic bags, apparel, hot peppers, limes, live plants and cattle. The value of imports totaled US$31.02 million (2016 est.), consisting primarily of machinery and transportation equipment, foodstuffs, manufactured goods, fuels and lubricants.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1979 to 1989, Montserrat was home to a branch of <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>'s <a href="/wiki/AIR_Studios" class="mw-redirect" title="AIR Studios">AIR Studios</a>, making the island popular with musicians who often went there to record while taking advantage of the island's climate and beautiful surroundings; the studio closed as a result of Hurricane Hugo.<sup id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Airport_(15632994595).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg/330px-Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg/440px-Montserrat_Airport_%2815632994595%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Airport_(15632994595).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>John A. Osborne Airport</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/John_A._Osborne_Airport" title="John A. Osborne Airport">John A. Osborne Airport</a> is the only airport on the island. Scheduled service to <a href="/wiki/V._C._Bird_International_Airport" title="V. C. Bird International Airport">Antigua</a> is provided by <a href="/wiki/FlyMontserrat" title="FlyMontserrat">FlyMontserrat</a><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/ABM_Air" title="ABM Air">ABM Air</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Charter flights are also available to the surrounding islands.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ferry service to the island is provided by the Jaden Sun Ferry. It runs from Heritage Quay in <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="St. John&#39;s, Antigua and Barbuda">St. John's, Antigua and Barbuda</a> to <a href="/wiki/Little_Bay,_Montserrat" title="Little Bay, Montserrat">
Little Bay</a> on Montserrat. The ride is about an hour and a half and operates five days a week.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Montserrat" title="Demographics of Montserrat">Demographics of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>The island had a population of 5,879 (according to a 2008 estimate). An estimated 8,000 refugees left the island (<a href="/wiki/Montserratians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Montserratians in the United Kingdom">primarily to the UK</a>) following the resumption of volcanic activity in July 1995; the population was 13,000 in 1994. The 2011 Montserrat census indicated a population of 4,922.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In early 2016, the estimated population had reached nearly 5,000 primarily due to immigration from other islands.<sup id="cite_ref-2016Pop_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Age structure (2003 estimates):
</p>
<ul><li>0–14 years: 23.4% (male 1,062; female 1,041)</li>
<li>15–64 years: 65.3% (male 2,805; female 3,066)</li>
<li>65 years and over: 11.3% (male 537; female 484)</li></ul>
<p>The median age of the population was 28.1 as of 2002 and the sex ratio was 0.96 males/female as of 2000.
</p><p>The population growth rate is 6.9% (2008 est.), with a birth rate of 17.57 births/1,000 population, death rate of 7.34 deaths/1,000 population (2003 est.), and net migration rate of 195.35/1,000 population (2000 est.) There is an infant mortality rate of 7.77 deaths/1,000 live births (2003 est.). The life expectancy at birth is 78.36 years: 76.24 for males and 80.59 for females (2003 est.). The total fertility rate is 1.8 children born/woman (2003 est.).
</p><p>According to a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimate, the population as of April 2018 was 5,197 (for a density of 52 per square kilometer or 135 people per square mile), with just over 90% living in non-urban areas.
<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, the CIA estimated the primary religion as Protestant (67.1%, including Anglican 21.8%, Methodist 17%, Pentecostal 14.1%, Seventh Day Adventist 10.5%, and Church of God 3.7%), with Roman Catholics constituting 11.6%, Rastafarian 1.4%, other 6.5%, none 2.6%, unspecified 10.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Residents of Montserrat are known as Montserratians. The population is predominantly, but not exclusively, of mixed African-Irish descent.<sup id="cite_ref-freepages.genealogy.rootsweb.ancestry.com_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freepages.genealogy.rootsweb.ancestry.com-78">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> It is not known with certainty how many African slaves and indentured Irish labourers were brought to the West Indies, though according to one estimate some 60,000 Irish were "Barbadosed" by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-yale.edu_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yale.edu-79">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> some of whom would have arrived in Montserrat.
</p><p>Data published by the <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">Central Intelligence Agency</a> indicates the ethnic group mix as follows (2011 est.):<sup id="cite_ref-cia.gov_50-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia.gov-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>African/black 88.4%</li>
<li>Mixed 3.7%</li>
<li>Hispanic/Spanish 3%</li>
<li>non-Hispanic Caucasian/white 2.7%</li>
<li>East Indian/Indian 1.5%</li>
<li>Other 0.7%</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Montserrat" title="Education in Montserrat">Education in Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Education in Montserrat is compulsory for children between the ages of 5 and 14, and free up to the age of 17. The only <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">secondary school</a> (pre-16 years of age) on the island is the <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Secondary_School" title="Montserrat Secondary School">Montserrat Secondary School</a> (MSS) in <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Montserrat" title="Salem, Montserrat">Salem</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-80">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_Community_College" title="Montserrat Community College">Montserrat Community College</a> (MCC) is a <a href="/wiki/Community_college" title="Community college">community college</a> (post-16 and tertiary educational institution) in Salem.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> maintains its Montserrat Open Campus.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Science,_Arts_and_Technology" title="University of Science, Arts and Technology">University of Science, Arts and Technology</a> is a private medical school in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Olveston,_Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Olveston, Montserrat (page does not exist)">Olveston</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Cultural_Center_(5809290561).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/220px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/330px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg/440px-Montserrat_Cultural_Center_%285809290561%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montserrat_Cultural_Center_(5809290561).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Montserrat Cultural Centre overlooking Little Bay</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Montserrat" title="Music of Montserrat">Music of Montserrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_West_Indies" title="Cricket in the West Indies">Cricket in the West Indies</a></div>
<table class="box-Essay-like plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-essay-like" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>is written like a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not#Wikipedia_is_not_a_publisher_of_original_thought" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">personal reflection, personal essay, or argumentative essay</a></b> that states a Wikipedia editor's personal feelings or presents an original argument about a topic.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit">help improve it</a> by rewriting it in an <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Writing_better_articles#Information_style_and_tone" title="Wikipedia:Writing better articles">encyclopedic style</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">May 2016</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>In 1979, <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">George Martin</a>, an English record producer, built a recording studio on the island called AIR Studios Montserrat. For more than a decade, AIR Montserrat played host to recording sessions by many well known rock musicians, including <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> In 1989, Hurricane Hugo destroyed the studios.
</p><p>After the volcanic eruptions of 1995 through 1997, and until his death in 2016, George Martin raised funds to help the victims and families on the island. The first event was a star-studded event at London's Royal Albert Hall in September 1997 (Music for Montserrat) featuring many artists who had previously recorded on the island including Paul McCartney, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a>, Elton John, <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, Phil Collins, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton" title="Eric Clapton">Eric Clapton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Midge_Ure" title="Midge Ure">Midge Ure</a>. All the proceeds from the show went towards short-term relief for the islanders.<sup id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Martin's second major initiative was to release five hundred limited edition lithographs of his score for the Beatles song "<a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(Beatles_song)" title="Yesterday (Beatles song)">Yesterday</a>". Complete with mistakes and tea stains, the lithographs are numbered and signed by Paul McCartney and Martin. The lithograph sale raised more than US$1.4 million which helped fund the building of a new cultural and community centre for Montserrat and provided a much needed focal point to help the re-generation of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_72-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many albums of note were recorded at <a href="/wiki/Associated_Independent_Recording" title="Associated Independent Recording">AIR Studios</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Brothers_in_Arms_(album)" title="Brothers in Arms (album)">Brothers in Arms</a></i>; <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_and_the_Ragged_Tiger" title="Seven and the Ragged Tiger">Seven and the Ragged Tiger</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">the Police</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Synchronicity_(The_Police_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Synchronicity (The Police album)">Synchronicity</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Ghost_in_the_Machine_(The_Police_album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghost in the Machine (The Police album)">Ghost in the Machine</a></i> (videos for "<a href="/wiki/Every_Little_Thing_She_Does_Is_Magic" title="Every Little Thing She Does Is Magic">Every Little Thing She Does Is Magic</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Spirits_in_the_Material_World" title="Spirits in the Material World">Spirits in the Material World</a>" were actually filmed in Montserrat), and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Buffett" title="Jimmy Buffett">Jimmy Buffett</a>'s <i>Volcano</i> (named for Soufrière Hills). After sustaining severe damage from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hugo" title="Hurricane Hugo">Hurricane Hugo</a> in 1989, the studio is now a ruin.<sup id="cite_ref-AirMonserrat_72-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AirMonserrat-72">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ian_Anderson" title="Ian Anderson">Ian Anderson</a> (of <a href="/wiki/Jethro_Tull_(band)" title="Jethro Tull (band)">Jethro Tull</a>) recorded the song "Montserrat" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_Language_of_Birds" title="The Secret Language of Birds">The Secret Language of Birds</a></i> in tribute to the volcanic difficulties and feeling among residents of being abandoned by the UK government.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has one national radio station, ZJB. The station offers a wide selection of music and news within the island and also on the internet for Montserratians living overseas.
</p><p>Notable shows include the <i>Morning Show</i> with Basil Chambers and Rose Willock's <i>Cultural Show</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Montserrat" title="Cuisine of Montserrat">Cuisine of Montserrat</a></div>
<p>Montserrat's national dish is <a href="/wiki/Goat_water" title="Goat water">goat water</a>, a thick goat meat stew served with crusty bread rolls.<sup id="cite_ref-2016Pop_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016Pop-10">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Montserrat cuisine resembles the general British and Caribbean cuisines, as it is situated in the Caribbean zone and it is a British territory. The cuisine includes a wide range of light meats, like fish, seafood and chicken, which are mostly grilled or roasted. Being a fusion of numerous cultures, such as Spanish, French, African, Indian and Amerindian, the Caribbean cuisine is unique and complex. More sophisticated meals include the Montserrat jerk shrimp, with rum, cinnamon bananas and cranberry. In other more rural areas, people prefer to eat homemade food, like the traditional mahi mahi and local breads.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Yachting">Yachting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Yachting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat is home to the Montserrat Yachting Association.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
