<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has competed in every <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">Basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Basketball is growing in popularity in Montserrat with the country now setting up their own basketball league.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The league contains six teams, which are the Look-Out Shooters, Davy Hill Ras Valley, Cudjoe Head Renegades, St. Peters Hilltop, Salem Jammers and MSS School Warriors.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> They have also built a new 800 seater complex which cost $1.5 million.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In common with many Caribbean islands, <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> is a very popular sport in Montserrat. Players from Montserrat are eligible to play for the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_cricket_team" title="West Indies cricket team">West Indies cricket team</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Allen_(cricketer)" title="Jim Allen (cricketer)">Jim Allen</a> was the first to play for the West Indies and he represented the <a href="/wiki/World_Series_Cricket" title="World Series Cricket">World Series Cricket</a> West Indians, although, with a very small population, no other player from Montserrat had gone on to represent the West Indies until <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Baker" title="Lionel Baker">Lionel Baker</a> made his One Day International debut against Pakistan in November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_cricket_team" title="Montserrat cricket team">Montserrat cricket team</a> forms a part of the <a href="/wiki/Leeward_Islands_cricket_team" title="Leeward Islands cricket team">Leeward Islands cricket team</a> in regional domestic cricket, however it plays as a separate entity in minor regional matches,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> as well having previously played <a href="/wiki/Twenty20" title="Twenty20">Twenty20</a> cricket in the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_20/20" title="Stanford 20/20">Stanford 20/20</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Two grounds on the island have held <a href="/wiki/First-class_cricket" title="First-class cricket">first-class</a> matches for the Leeward Islands, the first and most historic was <a href="/wiki/Sturge_Park" title="Sturge Park">Sturge Park</a> in Plymouth, which had been in use since the 1920s. This was destroyed in 1997 by the volcanic eruption. A new ground, the <a href="/wiki/Salem_Oval" title="Salem Oval">Salem Oval</a>, was constructed and opened in 2000. This has also held first-class cricket. A second ground has been constructed at Little Bay.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Montserrat has its own <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> affiliated <a href="/wiki/Montserrat_national_football_team" title="Montserrat national football team">football team</a>, and has competed in the World Cup qualifiers five times but failed to advance to the finals from 2002 to 2018. A field for the team was built near the airport by FIFA. In 2002, the team competed in a friendly match with the second-lowest-ranked team in FIFA at that time, <a href="/wiki/Bhutan_national_football_team" title="Bhutan national football team">Bhutan</a>, in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Final" title="The Other Final">The Other Final</a></i>, the same day as the final of the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2002 World Cup">2002 World Cup</a>. Bhutan won 4–0. Montserrat has failed to qualify for any <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a>. They have also failed to ever qualify for the <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF_Gold_Cup" title="CONCACAF Gold Cup">Gold Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Cup" title="Caribbean Cup">Caribbean Cup</a>. The current national team relies mostly on the <a href="/wiki/Diaspora" title="Diaspora">diaspora</a> resident in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and in the last WCQ against <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_national_football_team" title="Curaçao national football team">Curaçao</a> nearly all the squad members played and lived in England.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Surfing">Surfing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Surfing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Surfing was introduced by two American brothers in 1980, Carrll and Gary Robilotta. They were also responsible for naming the surfing spots on the island. Carrll wrote for the surfing newsletter <i>The Surf Report</i>, which was used by surfers around the globe. They both made Montserrat their home for 12 years.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">Settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay,_Montserrat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/220px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/330px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg/440px-Little_Bay%2C_Montserrat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Little_Bay,_Montserrat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Little Bay, the site of the new capital. The project was funded by the UK's <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Development" title="Department for International Development">Department for International Development</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Settlements known to be within the exclusion cannot be accessed and are no longer habitable. See also <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_abandoned_after_the_1997_Soufri%C3%A8re_Hills_eruption" class="mw-redirect" title="List of settlements abandoned after the 1997 Soufrière Hills eruption">List of settlements abandoned after the 1997 Soufrière Hills eruption</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements_in_the_safe_zone">Settlements in the safe zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Settlements in the safe zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abandoned_settlements_in_the_exclusion_zone">Abandoned settlements in the exclusion zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Abandoned settlements in the exclusion zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Settlements in italic have been destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Pyroclastic_flows" class="mw-redirect" title="Pyroclastic flows">pyroclastic flows</a> since the 1997 eruption. Others have been evacuated or destroyed since 1995.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_Montserratians">Notable Montserratians</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Notable Montserratians">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Allen_(cricketer)" title="Jim Allen (cricketer)">Jim Allen</a>, former cricketer who represented the <a href="/wiki/World_Series_Cricket" title="World Series Cricket">World Series Cricket</a> West Indians</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jennette_Arnold" title="Jennette Arnold">Jennette Arnold</a>, the first Montserratian elected as a Member of the <a href="/wiki/London_Assembly" title="London Assembly">London Assembly</a>, who served four terms as Chair of the Assembly</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lionel_Baker" title="Lionel Baker">Lionel Baker</a>, the first Montserratian to represent the West Indies in international cricket</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arrow_(musician)" title="Arrow (musician)">Alphonsus "Arrow" Cassell</a>, musician known for his <a href="/wiki/Soca_music" title="Soca music">soca</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Hot_Hot_Hot_(Arrow_song)" title="Hot Hot Hot (Arrow song)">Hot Hot Hot</a>"</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Farrell" title="Vladimir Farrell">Vladimir Farrell</a>, association footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Howard_A._Fergus" class="mw-redirect" title="Howard A. Fergus">Howard A. Fergus</a>, author, poet and three time acting <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Montserrat#Governors_of_Montserrat,_1971–present" title="Governor of Montserrat">governor of Montserrat</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Patricia_Griffin" title="Patricia Griffin">Patricia Griffin</a>, pioneer nurse and volunteer social worker, honored on a 2006 series of stamps recognizing notable citizens<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_Irish" title="George Irish">George Irish</a>, writer, human rights activist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/E._A._Markham" title="E. A. Markham">E. A. Markham</a>, poet and author</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dean_Mason" title="Dean Mason">Dean Mason</a>, association footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shane_Ryan_(social_activist)" title="Shane Ryan (social activist)">Shane Ryan</a>, writer, human rights activist</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/M._P._Shiel" title="M. P. Shiel">M. P. Shiel</a>, writer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyle_Taylor" title="Lyle Taylor">Lyle Taylor</a>, association footballer</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Maizie_Williams" title="Maizie Williams">Maizie Williams</a>, member of pop group <a href="/wiki/Boney_M" class="mw-redirect" title="Boney M">Boney M</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Angela_Yee" title="Angela Yee">Angela Yee</a>, member of Power 105.1's morning show, the Breakfast Club</li></ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montserrat&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-Plymouth-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Plymouth_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Plymouth_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Ghost_town" title="Ghost town">Abandoned</a> in 1997, following a volcanic eruption, although it is still the <i>de jure</i> capital.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Brades-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Brades_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Brades_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Government buildings are now located in Brades, making it the <i>de facto</i> capital.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-LittleBay-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-LittleBay_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-LittleBay_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">New seaport and town, intended to be the future capital.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Minister of State in the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">Foreign and Commonwealth Office</a> with responsibility for the British Overseas Territories.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes the <a href="/wiki/John_A._Osborne_Airport" title="John A. Osborne Airport">new airport</a> in the north of the island.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-De_Bhaldraithe-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_31-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-De_Bhaldraithe_31-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_de_Bhaldraithe" title="Tomás de Bhaldraithe">De Bhaldraithe, Tomás</a>, ed. "Entry 2700, 1 Aibreán 1831 [1 April 1831]". <i><a href="/wiki/C%C3%ADn_Lae_Amhlaoibh" title="Cín Lae Amhlaoibh">Cín Lae Amhlaoibh</a></i> (in Irish). <a href="/wiki/Baile_%C3%81tha_Cliath" class="mw-redirect" title="Baile Átha Cliath">Baile Átha Cliath</a>: An Clóchomhar Tta. p.&#160;84. <q>Is clos dom gurb í an teanga Ghaeilge is teanga mháthartha i Monserrat san India Thiar ó aimsir Olibher Cromaill, noch do dhíbir cuid de chlanna Gael ó Éirinn gusan Oileán sin Montserrat. Labhartar an Ghaeilge ann go coiteann le daoine dubha agus bána. [I heard that the Irish language is the mother tongue in Montserrat in the West Indies since the time of Oliver Cromwell, who banished some Gaelic Irish families there.
